--- Commit Message ---
LU-14677 sec: no encryption key migrate/extend/resync/split

Allow some layout operations on encrypted files, even when the
encryption key is not available:
- lfs migrate
- lfs mirror extend
- lfs mirror resync
- lfs mirror verify
- lfs mirror split
We allow these access patterns to applications that know what they are
doing, by using the specific flag O_FILE_ENC and O_DIRECT.

Also add sanity-sec test_59a,b,c to exercise these access patterns.

Signed-off-by: Sebastien Buisson <sbuisson@ddn.com>

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-06-17 21:52:40.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1: Code-Review-1

(19 comments)

--- Message (Sebastien Buisson, 2021-06-18 07:55:34.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

The implementation choice made in this patch to not force O_DIRECT was mainly due to the feature landed with patch https://review.whamcloud.com/40275, ie the ability to use buffered IO in mirror extend to improve performance.

If we consider it is fine performance-wise for now to just support O_DIRECT for encrypted files in case of migrate/extend/resync/split, then I would be happy to do it, because as you said there is always the risk of a buggy application that would leave ciphertext data in the page cache (although we do say O_FILE_ENC and O_FILE_ENC_NONDIRECT are only for applications that know what they are doing ;-) ).

Can you please confirm this is ok to restrict to O_DIRECT for now, before I update this patch? Thanks.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-06-18 08:23:59.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

Given that this is a new feature, I think we are free to implement the behavior that is best.

Given that the *current* behavior is "not working", this will be a significant improvement that it now works.  Also, Patrick's O_DIRECT optimization patches will almost certainly land together with this patch in the 2.15 release and improve O_DIRECT performance significantly, probably even faster than buffered IO, so I don't think it will be a problem to require O_DIRECT for copying encrypted files.

--- Message (Sebastien Buisson, 2021-06-18 08:51:42.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

(4 comments)

Thanks for your quick reply Andreas, I will update the patch accordingly.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-06-18 09:00:32.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

(1 comment)

--- Message (Sebastien Buisson, 2021-06-18 09:06:18.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

Now that I am thinking about it... One major drawback of forcing O_DIRECT for migrate/resync/extend/split on encrypted files is that it would need to be done for non-encrypted files as well. Or we would have to always call llapi_file_is_encrypted() *before* opening the file that is being migrated/resynced/extended/split, which means an additional open then ioctl then close.

So this extra costs bothers me. Do you see what I mean?

--- Message (Sebastien Buisson, 2021-06-18 11:59:47.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

> So this extra costs bothers me. Do you see what I mean?

What I can probably do to avoid this extra cost is to check for O_DIRECT on kernel side, instead of doing the pre-check in userspace.

- resync and verify natively use O_DIRECT, so they are fine.

- For migrate, we already forbid the use of the '--non-direct' option on encrypted files without the key, this is fine too.

- 'split -d' can easily be converted to make use of O_DIRECT for all files in all situations, and other forms of split are already not supported for encrypted files without the key.

- extend is more complicated. I should add a new '--force-direct' flag to the command, and allow mirror extend on encrypted files without the key only when this flag is specified.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-06-18 16:42:02.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

You wouldn't strictly need to "pre-check" files, since the open() would fail with -ENOKEY on encrypted files if the flag was not used. Then the O_FILE_ENC | O_DIRECT flags could be added and the open retried. Since this would apply to all files in that subdirectory, it could be cached for that directory traversal.

(1 comment)

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-08-01 16:06:12.000000000) ---
Patch Set 14:

Files can be migrated by the file owner or root. Allowing or preventing migration by requiring the encryption key does not improve security, and would probably weaken it.   If admin tools that are managing data (eg. automatic resync of stale files, or tools that balance storage between OSTs) would need to have an key that could decrypt *every* file in the filesystem, this would be a huge security risk. 

The premise of all modern encryption is that the data should be secure even if the cyohertext is accessible, and the encryption algorithm is known. The point of on-disk encryption in Lustre is that the data is safe even against someone that has direct access to the OSTs (at least to the extent possible), so having a key available on the servers to decrypt the file, only in order to move the data around, is contrary to this goal.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-08-01 16:08:00.000000000) ---
Patch Set 14:

PS: having a security review of the fscrypt feature in Lustre would be welcome, but it should be done on the whole fscrypt implementation, not on this patch in isolation

cached data is wiped once IOs are finished, for instance via fadvise."

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2021-12-10 15:54:55.000000000) ---
Patch Set 23:

The nonce is supposed to be unique within a communication, so an identical file the same nonce is just an extra copy of a message, which is obviously fine...

But if the file can be changed *separately*, as the mirrors can, then it's not quite right to re-use the nonce.  The implications are, as ever, complex, and probably a bit beyond me, but...

In general, a nonce is used to prevent replay attacks by guaranteeing the same data is not encrypted the same way in different messages.  In the case of mirrors, that's not a problem since we advertise whether or not they have the same contents.

Ah, but in the case of mirror split it is - because they are now different files and therefore must have different nonces.

Nice work, Sebastien :)

--- Message (Sebastien Buisson, 2021-12-10 16:44:53.000000000) ---
Patch Set 23:

(3 comments)

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-12-11 01:08:11.000000000) ---
Patch Set 23:

(1 comment)

My comment isn't a reason to deny this patch, since it is "safe" as is, but possibly just "too safe".  That said, I don't think many users split the mirror to a file, but mostly just delete the mirror immediately ("lfs mirror split -d" == "lfs mirror delete", which I guess was not backported to b_es5_2).
